The Rational Proof that the Servant is Not the Creator
Rational proof using conditional syllogism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof (conditional syllogism) used to demonstrate that the servant cannot be the creator of his actions.

Core Idea
If the servant created his actions, he would know all their details; he does not, so he is not the creator.

The author now presents a rational argument that complements the scriptural evidence. Using a conditional syllogism, he shows that the impossibility of the necessary consequence (detailed knowledge) proves the impossibility of the antecedent (servant as creator). This proof is subtle but clear to those who affirm divine unity.

Guided Path
1
Read the rational proof carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if...then...'.
Key terms: لازم (consequent), ملزوم (antecedent).
2
Identify the conditional statement
The author states: if the servant were the creator of his actions, then he would know all their details. This is the implication.
3
Understand why the consequent is false
The consequent (knowing all details) is false because humans do not have such knowledge. Therefore, the antecedent (servant as creator) is also false.
This is a modus tollens argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة كسب الأفعال غير أنْ يكونَ مُوجدا وخالقا لها ، وإِنَّما له فيها نسبة الترجيح، كالميل للفعل أو التّرك، والأصل في هذا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَخَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدَّرَهُ تَقْدِيرًا﴾ [الفرقان: 2] . ﴿ وَاللهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الصافات: 96] . ولو كانَ العبد خالِقا لأفعاله لكانَ عالما بتفاصيلها ، واللَّازِم باطل ؛ فالملزوم كذلكَ . فَلْتَعْرِفَا هذا الحُكْمَ الخَفِيَّ الإدراك ، مع ظهوره عند مُثبتِ الوحدانيّة المَحضَة له تعالى
The issue of the acquisition of actions: it is not that he is an originator and creator of them, but rather he has in them a proportion of preponderance, like inclination towards action or abandonment. The basis for this is the saying of the Most High: 'And He created everything and determined it with [precise] determination' [Al-Furqan: 2], 'And Allah created you and what you do' [As-Saffat: 96]. And if the servant were a creator of his actions, he would be knowing of their details, but the consequent is false, so the antecedent is likewise. So know, both of you, this judgment that is hidden in perception, while it is apparent to the establisher of pure unity for Him, Exalted.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage provides both transmitted and rational proof for the doctrine of kasb (acquisition). It begins by defining the issue: human action is not created by the servant, but the servant has an aspect of preponderance (tarjih) through inclination. Then it cites two Qur'anic verses as transmitted evidence. Then it presents a rational proof in the form of a conditional syllogism: if the servant were the creator of his actions, he would have detailed knowledge of them (a necessary implication), but the consequent is false (by experience, humans do not know all intricate details of their actions), hence the antecedent (the servant being creator) is also false. The conclusion is that the servant is not the creator. The author then addresses the reader (dual form 'fa'tarifa') to recognise this subtle judgment, which is clear to those who affirm pure divine unity.

Defining Ru'ya and Its Possibility
Sanusi defines ru'ya as a divine power and explains its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of ru'ya as a divinely created power, its possibility based on revealed evidence, and why it does not imply direction.

Core Idea
Ru'ya is not about optics; it is a power Allah grants, free from physical conditions.

This lesson introduces one of the most nuanced topics in kalam: the vision of Allah (ru'ya). Sanusi begins by defining ru'ya clearly—it is a power Allah places in creation, not dependent on physical conditions like rays or facing direction. He then explains that the everyday conditions are merely customary, not rational necessities, so ru'ya is possible. Finally, he addresses a key objection: if Allah is seen, does that place Him in a direction? Sanusi decisively answers that believers see Him without direction, just as they know He is without direction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Let the author's own words set the framework before we analyze.
The passage contains important distinctions, so read carefully.
2
Identify the definition of ru'ya
Find the sentence where Sanusi defines ru'ya. Notice that he calls it a 'power' (quwwa) placed by Allah, not a natural process.
This definition is the foundation for the entire discussion.
3
Distinguish rational and customary conditions
Sanusi says that ordinary vision requires rays and facing the object, but these are customary, not rational necessities. Understand this key distinction.
If they were rational conditions, ru'ya would be impossible. Since they are customary, ru'ya is possible.
4
Grasp the proof from revelation
The passage states that ru'ya is permissible because it is possible by evidence from revelation (sam'). Identify what that evidence is (referred to in the poem 'since it is attached to possibility').
This shows that ru'ya is known through scripture, not pure reason.
5
Appreciate the refutation of direction
Finally, Sanusi addresses an objection: if Allah is seen, He must be in a direction. He firmly denies this, explaining that believers see Him without direction (la fi jiha).
This guards against anthropomorphism and aligns with the Islamic creed that Allah is not in a place.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحَقُّ: قُوَّةٌ يَجْعَلُهَا اللَّهُ تَعَالَى فِي خَلْقِهِ، لَا يُشْتَرَطُ فِيهَا اتِّصَالُ الأَشِعَّةِ، وَلَا مُقَابَلَةُ المَرْئِيِّ، وَلَا غَيْرُ ذَلِكَ، وَلَكِنْ جَرَتِ العَادَةُ فِي رُؤْيَةِ بَعْضِنَا بَعْضًا بِوُجُودِ ذَلِكَ، عَلَى جِهَةِ الاتِّفَاقِ، لَا عَلَى سَبِيلِ الاشْتِرَاطِ (۱)؛ فَلَذَا كَانَتِ الرُّؤْيَةُ جَائِزَةً (۲) لِإِمْكَانِهَا بِدَلِيلِ السَّمْعِ (۳) المُشَارِ إِلَيْهِ بِقَوْلِهِ: (إِذْ بِجَائِزٍ عُلِّقَتْ) وَلَا يَلْزَمُ مِنْ رُؤْيَتِهِ تَعَالَى إِثْبَاتُ جِهَةٍ (٤) تَعَالَى اللَّهُ عَنْ ذَلِكَ عُلُوًّا كَبِيرًا! بَلْ جِهَةٍ(٤) يَرَاهُ المُؤْمِنُونَ لَا فِي جِهَةٍ، كَمَا يَعْلَمُونَ أَنَّهُ لَا فِي جِهَةٍ.
The truth: [ru'ya is] a power that Allah the Exalted places in His creation; connection of rays is not required in it, nor facing the seen object, nor anything else. But customarily, in seeing one another, these exist as a matter of agreement, not as a condition; therefore ru'ya is permissible, because it is possible by the evidence of the Revealed (sam') alluded to by His saying: 'since it is attached to possibility.' And from seeing Him the Exalted, no direction is necessitated—far exalted is Allah above that, a great exaltation! Rather, the believers see Him without direction, just as they know that He is without direction.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage defines ru'ya (vision of Allah) and affirms its possibility for the believers. The author begins by defining the reality of ru'ya: it is a power (quwwa) that Allah creates in His creatures. He then clarifies the conditions of ordinary vision: connection of rays, facing the object, etc. These are not rationally required (shart 'aqli) but merely customary (shart 'adi); they exist by agreement (ittifaq) in this world but are not necessary for ru'ya itself. Therefore ru'ya is possible (ja'iz) and in fact is attested by revealed evidence (dalil al-sam'), namely the verse alluded to from Jawharat al-Tawhid. The author then addresses a common objection: if Allah is seen, He must be in a direction. He firmly denies this, stating that believers see Him without direction (la fi jiha), just as they know He is without direction. This guards against anthropomorphism (tashbih).

Key Terms
رؤية (ru'ya)
قوة (quwwa)
شرط عقلي (shart 'aqli)
شرط عادي (shart 'adi)
جهة (jiha)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That ru'ya requires physical direction and that seeing Allah would necessitate Him being in a place.
Correction: The passage clarifies that ru'ya is a power not dependent on physical conditions, and that believers see Allah without direction (la fi jiha), just as they know He is without direction.

Checkpoint
What is the definition of ru'ya according to this passage?
A) It is the connection of rays from the eye to the object.
B) It is a power that Allah places in His creation, not requiring customary conditions for its possibility.
C) It is facing the seen object.
D) It is necessarily conditioned by direction and place.

Key Takeaway
Ru'ya is a divinely granted power, possible by revelation, and does not imply direction for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson teaches that ru'ya is a power Allah grants, not dependent on your physical senses. Do you live as if you truly expect to see Allah in the Hereafter, or have you reduced your relationship with Him to what you can perceive now? What would change if you genuinely anticipated that vision today?
?
The author distinguishes customary conditions from rational ones. Are there 'customary conditions' you have placed on your worship—like needing a certain feeling or circumstance—that have become barriers to relying on Allah's power alone? How can you strip them away?
?
If ru'ya is possible only by revelation, how much do you depend on revealed knowledge for your understanding of the unseen? Is there an area where your intellect or culture has led you to doubt what Allah's word clearly teaches? Repent and submit.

Refuting the Mu'tazilite Objection to Seeing Allah
Sanusi presents and answers the Mu'tazilite rational objection from direction and facing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the strongest rational argument the Mu'tazilites posed against ru'ya and how the Ash'ari response resolves it by denying physical modalities.

Core Idea
Ru'ya is free from the conditions of physical sight.

This lesson tackles the most challenging rational objection to the reality of seeing Allah in the hereafter. The Mu'tazilites argued that sight necessarily requires direction, space, and distance—impossible for Allah. Sanusi presents their argument and then gives the decisive Ash'ari answer: ru'ya is 'bila kayf', a direct perception created by Allah without any physical modality.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: first the objection (doubt), then the answer.
Footnote markers like (٥) refer to glosses; ignore them for the core argument.
2
Identify the premises of the Mu'tazilite argument
The Mu'tazilites argue that sight implies direction, place, and distance. If Allah were seen, He would be facing the seer, thus in a direction and space. That would make Him either a substance or an accident, and either limited or divisible.
This is called shubhat al-muqabala (the doubt of facing).
3
Understand the Ash'ari answer
The answer is that ru'ya is 'bila kayf' (without modality). This means it is free from facing, direction, specific distance, and encompassing. Ru'ya is a type of perception (idrak) that Allah creates directly, whenever He wills.
The answer does not deny the reality of vision; it denies the physical conditions.
4
Reflect on the term 'bila kayf'
Consider how the term 'bila kayf' preserves Allah's transcendence while affirming the possibility of seeing Him in the afterlife. It is a key principle in Ash'ari theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخالف في ذلك جميعُ الفِرَق (٥)، فأحالها المعتزلة، بناء على أنَّها لا تتعلق عقلا إلا بما هو في جهةٍ، ومكانٍ، ومسافة مخصوصة (٦)، متمسكين بِشُبَه عَقليَّةٍ، أقواها: شُبهة المُقابلة، وتقريرها: أنَّه تعالى لو كان مَرئيًّا لكان مُقابِلًا للرَّائي بالضرورة؛ فيكون في جهةٍ وحيِّز، وهو مُحالٌ، ولَكانَ إِمَّا جوهرًا أو عَرَضًا (۱)؛ لأنَّ المُتحيِّز بالاستقلال جوهر، أو بالتبعية عَرَض، ولَكانَ المَرئى إمّا كُلَّه، فيكونُ محدوداً متناهيا محصوراً، وإمَّا بعضه فيكونُ مُتَبَعِّضًا مُتَجَزِّئًا إلى غير ذلك، وهذه الشُّبهة أشار إلى جوابها بقوله: (لَكِنْ) النَّظَرُ الحاصل بحاسة البصر للرَّائين (بِلَا كَيْف) أي: تَكَيُّف للمرئي مِن مقابلةٍ، وجهة، ومسافة مخصوصة، وإحاطة به، بل يجب تَجرُّده عنه؛ فإنَّ الرُّؤية نوع من الإدراك يخلقه الله تعالى متى شاء، ولأي شيء شاء (۲)؛ فالمراد بالمُخالفة في الكيف وجوبُ خُلو رؤية الواجب تعالى عن الشَّرائطِ والكيفيات المُعتبَرة في رؤية الأجسام والأعراض.
And all sects disagreed concerning that; the Mu'tazilites deemed it impossible, based on the fact that sight is rationally related only to what is in a direction, place, and specific distance, holding to rational doubts, the strongest of which is the doubt of facing (shubhat al-muqabala). Its formulation: that if the Exalted were seen, He would necessarily be facing the seer; thus He would be in a direction and a space, which is impossible; and He would be either a substance or an accident because whatever occupies space independently is a substance, or dependently it is an accident; and the seen object would be either entirely [visible], so it would be limited, finite, and confined, or partly visible, so it would be divisible and fragmented, etc. This doubt [the author] pointed to its answer by his saying: 'But the vision occurring through the sense of sight for the seers (bila kayf) i.e., without any modality for the seen object from facing, direction, specific distance, or encompassing; rather, it must be free of that. For ru'ya is a type of perception that Allah creates whenever He wills and for whatever He wills. So what is meant by 'differing in modality' is the necessity of the vision of the Necessary Being being free from the conditions and modalities considered in the vision of bodies and accidents.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the strongest Mu'tazilite rational objection against ru'ya, known as shubhat al-muqabala (the doubt of facing). The author first notes that the Mu'tazilites deny ru'ya because they consider sight to be rationally conditioned by direction, place, and distance. Their strongest argument is: if Allah were seen, He would have to be opposite the seer, thus in a direction and space—impossible for Allah. Moreover, whatever occupies space is either a substance or an accident, and the seen object would have to be either entirely visible (implying limitation) or partly visible (implying divisibility). The author then provides the answer, referencing the text of Jawharat al-Tawhid: ru'ya is 'bila kayf' (without modality). This means that it is free from conditions like facing, direction, specific distance, and encompassing. Ru'ya is simply a type of perception (idrak) that Allah creates directly, whenever and for whomever He wills. Therefore, the vision of Allah is free from the modalities that apply to physical bodies and accidents.

Key Terms
المعتزلة (al-Mu'tazila)
شبهة المقابلة (shubhat al-muqabala)
بلا كيف (bila kayf)
جوهر (jawhar)
عَرَض ('arad)
إدراك (idrak)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ru'ya of Allah would require Him to be in a direction and be limited or divisible like physical objects.
Correction: Ru'ya is a type of perception (idrak) that Allah creates without any physical modality; it is free from facing, direction, distance, and encompassing.

Checkpoint
What is the core premise of the Mu'tazilite rational objection (shubhat al-muqabala)?
A) Allah cannot be seen because He is not in a direction.
B) Allah cannot be seen because seeing requires the seen object to be in a direction, place, and distance.
C) Allah cannot be seen because He is a substance.
D) Allah cannot be seen because He is an accident.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite objection fails because ru'ya is not subject to the physical conditions of direction, place, and distance; it is a direct perception (idrak) created by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine seeing Allah in Paradise, do you unconsciously picture a physical scene with direction and distance? How does the concept of 'bila kayf' confront that imagination? What must you change in your heart to truly believe in a vision without modality?
?
Are there areas in your aqeedah where you impose physical or human limitations on Allah without realizing it? What specific steps will you take to purify your belief in Allah's tanzih (transcendence) after learning that ru'ya is free from all conditions?
?
The Mu'tazilites rejected ru'ya because their reason could not conceive of sight without direction. Do you ever let your limited reason override what Allah has informed you about His attributes? How can you train your mind to accept the revealed truths even when they seem paradoxical?

Sending Messengers is Intellectually Permissible
Al-Malali defines the intellectual permissibility of sending messengers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Sunna consider sending messengers intellectually permissible (jā'iz 'aqlī) and how this differs from obligating or deeming it impossible.

Core Idea
Allah's sending messengers is His pure grace, not a duty.

This passage from al-Malali's Jawharat al-Tawhid establishes a key distinction in Islamic theology: sending messengers is not obligatory for Allah, nor is it impossible. Rather, it belongs to the category of the intellectually permissible—an act that reason considers equally possible to do or leave. The author roots this in the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna and uses it to refute two extreme positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic verse and translation
Read the verse carefully. Notice its structure: it directly states that sending messengers is from the permissible and negates obligation.
The verse uses 'fala wujūb' to negate obligation.
2
Understand the definition of jā'iz 'aqlī
The commentary defines jā'iz 'aqlī as that which reason permits to do or leave. This means it is neither obligatory nor impossible. Grasp this definition well.
This is a core concept in kalam.
3
See how this refutes two groups
The passage concludes that this position refutes two groups. Consider which groups those might be: those who say sending messengers is obligatory, and those who say it is impossible.
The author does not name them, but they are implied.
4
Reflect on the significance
Think about why this matters: it upholds Allah's complete freedom and grace. He is not compelled to send messengers, but does so out of mercy.
This highlights Tawhid and divine will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهُ إِرْسَالُ جَمِيعِ الرُّسْلِ فَلَا وُجُوبَ بَلْ بِمَحْضِ الفَضْلِ
ولما فرغ من الإلهيَّات شرَع في النُّبوَّات (۱) فقال: (وَمِنْهُ) أي: ومن أفراد (1)
يريد المصنف أنْ يُقرِّرَ أنَّ مذهب أهل السُّنَّة والجماعة: أنَّ مِن أنواع الجائز العقلي على الله تعالى إرساله لجميع الرُّسل مِن لَدُن آدمَ أبي البشر إلى خاتمهم وسيدهم محمد صلى الله عليه وعليهم أجمعين ، ومعنى ذلك أنَّ الإرسال مما هو ذلك أنَّ الإرسال مما هو جائز عقلا على الله تعالى عند أهل السُّنَّة أي: أنه لا يجب على الله تعالى إرسالهم ، ولا يستحيل عليه إرسالهم ؛ إذ الجائز العقلي هو ما يُجَوِّزُ العقل فعله وتركه ، ومتى جوّز فعله لم يكن تركه واجباً، ومتى جوز تركه لم يكن فعله واجبا، وفي هذا الكلام ردُّ على طائفتين من أهل البحث
From it (i.e., from the types of the intellectually permissible) is the sending of all messengers, so there is no obligation, rather by pure grace. And when he finished from the divine matters, he began with prophecies and said: (And from it) meaning: from the individuals (1). He (the author) intends to establish that the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a is that among the types of the intellectually permissible (al-jā'iz al-'aqlī) concerning Allah is His sending of all messengers from Adam, the father of humanity, to their seal and master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and them all. And the meaning of that is that the sending is intellectually permissible (jā'iz 'aqlī) concerning Allah according to Ahl al-Sunna, i.e., it is not obligatory upon Allah to send them, nor is it impossible for Him to send them; for the intellectually permissible is that which the intellect considers as permissible to do or to leave. And whenever it considers its doing permissible, its leaving is not obligatory, and whenever it considers its leaving permissible, its doing is not obligatory. And in this speech is a refutation of two groups of researchers.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal definition. It begins by quoting the author's verse: 'وَمِنْهُ إِرْسَالُ جَمِيعِ الرُّسْلِ فَلَا وُجُوبَ بَلْ بِمَحْضِ الفَضْلِ' which states that sending messengers is an instance of the intellectually permissible (al-jā'iz al-'aqli). The commentator explains that the author is establishing the position of Ahl al-Sunna: sending messengers is jā'iz 'aqlī, meaning it is not obligatory (wājib) nor impossible (mustaḥīl) for Allah. He defines jā'iz 'aqlī as that which the intellect allows either doing or leaving. If the intellect permits the act, then leaving it is not obligatory; if it permits leaving, then doing it is not obligatory. This shows the balance. Finally, he notes that this statement refutes two opposing groups: those who say it is obligatory and those who say it is impossible.

Key Terms
جائز عقلي
وجوب
استحالة
أهل السنة والجماعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think jā'iz 'aqlī means merely possible in a neutral sense, without negating obligation or impossibility.
Correction: Jā'iz 'aqlī explicitly negates both obligation and impossibility; it is a balanced rational judgment.

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Sunna, what is the rational judgment regarding Allah's sending of messengers?
A) Obligatory
B) Impossible
C) Permissible
D) Both obligatory and impossible

Key Takeaway
Allah's sending of messengers is an act of pure grace, intellectually permissible, not obligatory nor impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The intellect says it is possible for Allah to have left us without guidance. Knowing that He instead chose to guide us, what responsibility does that place on you to live according to that guidance? Will you commit today to acting on what you know of His message?

Types of Abrogation (Naskh) in the Quran and Sunnah
The commentator enumerates the three types of naskh with examples and a concluding note.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three types of abrogation (naskh) that occur in the Quran and Sunnah, along with key examples.

Core Idea
Abrogation in Islamic scripture comes in three forms: affecting recitation, ruling, or both.

In this passage, the commentator outlines the various ways abrogation (naskh) can occur. Before delving into specific examples, it is crucial to grasp these categories, as they are foundational to understanding how certain verses and rulings were superseded. The passage provides concrete cases from the Quran and hadith to illustrate each type.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of naskh
Read the passage and list the three categories of abrogation mentioned: (1) abrogation of both recitation and ruling, (2) abrogation of recitation only, (3) abrogation of ruling only.
These categories are distinct and each has examples.
2
Understand the example of abrogation by Sunnah
Note the claim that abrogation by a non-mutawatir hadith is not valid; only mutawatir Sunnah abrogates the Quran. Consider the example of bequest verses.
3
Examine the example for each type
Match each category with its example: for both recitation and ruling, ten breastfeedings; for recitation only, stoning verse; for ruling only, bequest for widows.
4
Reflect on the concluding remarks
Read Al-Shanwani's clarification about the permissibility of bequests and how the ruling changed.
This shows the practical application of naskh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنواع النسخ
إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ إِن تَرَكَ خَيْرًا الْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْوَالِدَيْنِ وَالْأَقْرَبِينَ [البقرة: 180] بحديث: لَا وَصِيَّةَ لِوَارِثٍ (1) والحقُّ أَنَّه لم يقع إلَّا بالسُّنَّة المتواترة (2).
كما شَمِل أيضا ما نُسخت تلاوته وحكمه جميعاً نحو: «عشر رضعات مُحرّماتٍ كان ممَّا يتلى فنُسخن بخمس معلومات (3).
وما نُسخت تلاوته دون حكمه (4) نحو: «الشيخ والشيخة (5) إذا زَنَيا فارجُموهما البيَّة نَكالا من الله والله عزيز حكيم كانَ ممَّا يُتلى فَرجَمَ النَّبِيُّ المحصنين.
وما نُسخ حكمه دون تلاوته كآية: وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا وَصِيَّةً لِّأَزْوَاجِهِم [البقرة: 240] نُسخ بأربعة أشهر وعشرا.
فلعل مراده بالجواز عدم الحرمة، لأنه كان في صدر الإسلام عدم حرمة التنفيذ للوصية بالنسبة للوالدين وإن لم يُجز بقية الورثة كالزوج، والآن يحرم التنفيذ إن لم يجز بقية الورثة كالزوج، فالوصية الآن صحيحة متوقف تنفيذها على إجازة بقية الورثة. الشنواني.
(1) أخرجه أبو داود والترمذي وابن ماجه كلهم في كتاب الوصايا. (2) قوله: (والحق أنه .. الخ) الكلام الآن في الوقوع، وعدمه، وما تقدم في الجواز، ولا نسلم عدم تواتر (لا) وصية لوارث بل هو متواتر عند المجتهدين الحاكمين بالنسخ. الشنواني. (3) صحيح مسلم، باب التحريم بخمس رضعات، رقم (3587) وسنن أبي داود، باب هل يحرم ما دون خمس رضعات، رقم (2062) ولفظه عندهما: «عشر رضعات يحرمن ثم نسخن بخمس معلومات يحرمن، فتوفي النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهن مما يقرأ من القرآن». والحديث عند غيرهما أيضا، ولم أجده بلفظ الشارح: عشر رضعات محرمات. (4) قوله: (وما نُسخت تلاوته دون حكمه إن قلت: لا يدخل هذا في تعريفه السابق بأنه رفع قلتُ: مرجعه نسخ ثبوت أحكام القرآنية للمتلو. الأمير. (5) قوله: (الشيخ والشيخة المراد: المحصن والمحصنة، سواء كانا شابين أو شيخين. الشنواني.
Types of Abrogation. When death approaches one of you, if he leaves wealth, the bequest is for parents and near relatives [Quran 2:180] (is abrogated) by the hadith: 'No bequest to an heir' (1). And the truth is that it (abrogation) did not occur except by the mutawatir sunnah (2). It also includes what was abrogated in its recitation and ruling altogether, like: 'Ten breastfeedings that are prohibited' used to be recited, then they were abrogated by five well-known (3). And what was abrogated in its recitation but not its ruling (4), like: 'The old man and old woman (5) when they commit adultery, stone them both as a punishment from Allah and Allah is Mighty, Wise' used to be recited, then the Prophet stoned the muhsan. And what was abrogated in its ruling but not its recitation, like the verse: 'And those who are taken in death among you and leave wives, a bequest for their wives' [Quran 2:240] abrogated by four months and ten (days). Perhaps his intent by permissibility is the absence of prohibition, because in early Islam there was no prohibition of executing the bequest for parents even if the remaining heirs did not permit it, like the husband, and now executing is prohibited if the remaining heirs do not permit it, like the husband. So the bequest now is valid, its execution dependent on the permission of the remaining heirs. Al-Shanwani. (1) Reported by Abu Dawood, al-Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah, all in the book of bequests. (2) His saying: (The truth is that... etc.) The discussion now is about occurrence and non-occurrence, and what preceded was about permissibility. And we do not accept the non-tawatur of 'No bequest to an heir'; rather it is mutawatir among the mujtahids who rule by abrogation. Al-Shanwani. (3) Sahih Muslim, chapter on prohibition by five breastfeedings, no. (3587) and Sunan Abi Dawood, chapter on whether less than five breastfeedings are prohibited, no. (2062), and its wording in both: 'Ten breastfeedings are prohibited, then they were abrogated by five well-known that are prohibited, and the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, passed away while they were among what is recited from the Quran.' The hadith is also with others, and I did not find it with the commentator's wording: 'ten prohibited breastfeedings'. (4) His saying: (What was abrogated in its recitation but not its ruling: if you say: this does not enter into his previous definition that it is a removal, I say: its reference is the abrogation of the establishment of Quranic rulings for the recited matter. Al-Amir. (5) His saying: (The old man and old woman) meaning the muhsan and muhsana, whether they are young or old. Al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage defines the types of abrogation (naskh) as understood in Sunni theology. The commentator first gives an example of abrogation by the Sunnah: the verse on bequests is abrogated by the hadith 'No bequest to an heir,' but the true view is that such abrogation only occurs via mutawatir Sunnah. Then he enumerates three types: (1) abrogation of both recitation and ruling, exemplified by the verse on ten breastfeedings; (2) abrogation of recitation but not ruling, exemplified by the verse on stoning the muhsan; (3) abrogation of ruling but not recitation, exemplified by the verse on bequest for widows abrogated by 'four months and ten.' The passage ends with Al-Shanwani's clarification on the permissibility of bequests in early Islam versus later ruling. Each type is supported by footnotes providing hadith references and commentary on nuances.

Key Terms
النسخ
التلاوة
الحكم
السنة المتواترة
الوصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abrogation implies alteration or change in Allah's speech itself.
Correction: Abrogation is a removal of the ruling or recitation according to divine wisdom, not a change in Allah's speech, which is eternal.

Checkpoint
What are the three types of abrogation (naskh) mentioned in the passage?
A) Abrogation of recitation only, ruling only, and both
B) Abrogation by Quran, Sunnah, and consensus
C) Abrogation of explicit commands, prohibitions, and stories
D) Abrogation of legal rulings, moral teachings, and eschatological matters

Key Takeaway
Abrogation in the Quran and Sunnah occurs in three ways: affecting recitation, ruling, or both, each with distinct examples.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that a Quranic verse can be abrogated in ruling while its recitation remains, like the bequest for widows. When you recite that verse, does it feel real to you that its ruling is no longer applicable? How does that affect your relationship with the Quran? Are you willing to accept that some verses are for recitation only, not for practice, as an act of submission to Allah's wisdom? Commit to memorizing at least one such verse and reflecting on the lesson of abrogation every time you recite it.
?
The hadith 'No bequest to an heir' abrogates a clear Quranic verse. Have you ever prioritized a personal desire over a clear Sunnah ruling, thinking it contradicts your interpretation of the Quran? This lesson shows that the Prophet's Sunnah, when mutawatir, carries decisive authority. Will you examine your own practices to ensure you are not following your own reasoning over the authentic Sunnah? Make a pact to seek knowledge of the Sunnah before making judgments on inheritance or other matters.
?
The abrogation of the stoning verse in recitation but not ruling means that a punishment commanded by Allah is not explicitly in the Quran today. Does this challenge your assumption that everything in Islam must be directly from the Quran? Are you comfortable with the Sunnah as a source of rulings that are not in the Quran? Reflect on your level of trust in the Prophet's teachings. Decide today to increase your study of hadith, especially those dealing with hudud punishments, so that you accept them fully as part of Allah's law.

Ash'ari Proof for the Permissibility of Divine Forgiveness
Ash'ari proof for the permissibility of forgiveness, rational and scriptural.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and scriptural basis for the Ash'ari position that divine forgiveness is permissible.

Core Idea
Forgiveness is God's right to grant, not an obligation.

The Ash'ari scholars provide a concise proof for why God's forgiveness is permissible. They combine a rational argument—punishment is God's right, so He may waive it—with three Quranic verses that show forgiveness actually occurs. This lesson unpacks that proof and clarifies what it means for God's justice and mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the logical flow: first the rational claim, then the scriptural evidence.
The proof is short but packed.
2
Examine the rational argument
The key point: punishment is God's right, not a debt owed to anyone else. Therefore, He may choose to forgive without injustice.
This guards against thinking forgiveness is obligatory.
3
Reflect on the Quranic verses
The three verses show that forgiveness is not only possible but actual. Note the exception for shirk in An-Nisa 48.
The verses support both permissibility and occurrence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
احتج أصحابنا على جواز العفو: بأن العقاب حقه تعالى، فيحسن إسقاطه، مع أن فيه نفعا للعبد من غير ضرر لأحد، وفي القرآن: ﴿وَهُوَ الَّذِى يَقْبَلُ التَّوْبَةَ عَنْ عِبَادِهِ، وَيَعْفُوا عَنِ السَّيِّئَاتِ ﴾ [الشورى: ٢٥]. ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَغْفِرُ الذُّنُوبَ جَمِيعًا ﴾ [الزمر: ٥٣]. ﴿ إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَن يُشْرَكَ بِهِ، وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَن يَشَاءُ ﴾ [النساء: ٤٨].
Our companions argued for the permissibility of forgiveness: because punishment is His right, exalted, so it is fitting to drop it, while it contains benefit for the servant without harm to anyone, and in the Quran: 'And He is the One who accepts repentance from His servants and pardons misdeeds' (Ash-Shura 25); 'Indeed, Allah forgives all sins' (Az-Zumar 53); 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that association be made with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' (An-Nisa 48).
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage presents the proof of the Ash'ari scholars for the permissibility of divine forgiveness. The proof has a rational component and a scriptural component. The rational component is that since punishment is a right belonging to God, it is fitting (حسن) for Him to remit it (إسقاطه). Moreover, forgiveness benefits the servant without causing harm to anyone. The scriptural component consists of three Quranic verses: the first from Ash-Shura 25 affirms that God accepts repentance and pardons misdeeds; the second from Az-Zumar 53 states that God forgives all sins; the third from An-Nisa 48 specifies that God does not forgive shirk but forgives what is less for whom He wills. These verses provide evidence not only for the permissibility but also for the actual occurrence of forgiveness.

Key Terms
احتج
جواز العفو
العقاب حقه
إسقاط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that forgiveness is obligatory upon God.
Correction: The proof shows that punishment is God's right, so He may exercise it or waive it; forgiveness is a gift, not a duty.

Checkpoint
What is the rational basis for the permissibility of forgiveness according to the Ash'aris?
A) God is obligated to forgive.
B) Punishment is unjust.
C) Punishment is God's right, so it is fitting to drop it, benefiting the servant without harming anyone.
D) Forgiveness is impossible.

Key Takeaway
Divine forgiveness is permissible because punishment is God's right, and He may remit it for the benefit of the servant, as confirmed by multiple Quranic verses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If forgiveness is God’s right and not an obligation, do you realize that every sin you have committed is met with grace if He forgives? How does that make you feel about His mercy—do you take it for granted?
?
The proof says forgiveness benefits you without harming anyone. Have you ever truly felt the weight of that benefit? How would your life change if you stopped treating God’s forgiveness as a casual transaction?
?
God forgives all sins except shirk (associating partners with Him). What hidden forms of shirk might exist in your heart—like seeking praise or relying on your own deeds—that you need to repent from?

Defining 'Thing' as Existent
Sanusi defines 'thing' as existent and asserts the impossibility of an intermediate state.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that 'thing' is synonymous with 'existent' and that there is no intermediate state between existence and non-existence, as established by rational necessity.

Core Idea
'Thing' and 'existent' are coextensive; non-existence is absolute nothingness.

This lesson introduces the foundational semantic axiom of Sunni theology: the term 'thing' applies only to what exists. The matn asserts that non-existence, whether possible or impossible, is not a thing and has no external fixity. It also tells us that there is no middle ground between existence and non-existence, and that this judgment is known by necessity.

Guided Path
1
Read the basic equation
Read the opening lines: 'كل شيء موجود، وكل موجود شيء' – notice that this is a two-way equivalence between 'thing' and 'existent'.
This is the central claim of the passage.
2
Understand the denial of non-existence
The matn then says the non-existent (whether possible or impossible) is not a thing and not fixed externally. Do you see why?
The reason given: existence is the very reality.
3
Grasp the necessity claim
The passage ends this section by saying this judgment is known 'by necessity' – meaning it is self-evident. Ponder why this is considered necessary.
Think: can you conceive of something that is neither existent nor non-existent?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات. فكل شيء موجود، وكل موجود شيء، والمعدوم مطلقا ـ ممكنا كان أو ممتنعا ـ ليس بشيء، ولا ثابت في الخارج؛ لأن الوجود نفس الحقيقة، فرفعه رفعها، ولا واسطة بين الموجود والمعدوم، وهذا الحكم ثابت عندنا بالضرورة؛ فإنها قاضية بذلك، إذ لا يعقل من الثبوت إلا الوجود خارجا أو ذهنا، ولا من العدم إلا نفي الوجود كذلك.
وقوله: (والمعدوم مطلقا) اختلف هل الأشياء قبل وجودها ثابتة في نفس الأمر وطرأ عليها الوجود؛ فهي قديمة والقدرة لم تتعلق إلا بوجودها وإظهارها، أو أنها قبل وجودها لم يكن لها ثبوت في نفس الأمر، بل كانت معدومة وتعلقت القدرة بإيجاد ذواتها؟ فذهبت المعتزلة إلى الأول، فقالوا: الحقائق الممكنة ليست بجعل جاعل، بل الحقيقة ثابتة في نفسها إلا أنها مستترة كاستتار المتاع في الصندوق، فهي ثابتة قبل وجودها وتعلقت القدرة بوجودها وظهورها، وإلى الثاني ذهب أهل السنة فقالوا: إن الحقائق بجعل جاعل، فهي معدومة ولا ثبوت لها قبل وجودها. والشارح رد على المعتزلة بقوله: والمعدوم مطلقا ليس بشيء خلافا للمعتزلة، فإن المعدوم عندهم شيء، لأن حقيقة المعدوم ثابتة في نفسها فليست معدوما صرفا ولا موجودا صرفا، فعندهم الثبوت في الخارج قد يجامع الوجود وقد لا يجامعه، بخلافه عند أهل السنة فإن الثابت في نفسه موجود في الخارج على التحقيق من نفي الأحوال.
Section of the Sam'iyyat. Every thing is existent, and every existent is a thing, and the non-existent absolutely — whether possible or impossible — is not a thing, nor is it fixed in external existence; because existence is the very reality, so its removal is its removal, and there is no intermediate between the existent and the non-existent, and this judgment is established with us by necessity; for necessity judges that, since no fixity is conceivable except existence externally or mentally, nor non-existence except negation of existence likewise.
And his saying: 'and the non-existent absolutely' — there is disagreement: Are things before their existence fixed in themselves and existence supervened upon them, so they are eternal and power is only connected with their existence and manifestation? Or were they before their existence not fixed in themselves, but rather non-existent, and power is connected with bringing their essences into existence? The Mu'tazila went to the first view, saying: The possible realities are not by a maker, but the reality is fixed in itself except that it is hidden like the hiding of goods in a chest; thus they are fixed before their existence and power is connected with their existence and manifestation. And the Ahl al-Sunna went to the second view, saying: Realities are by a maker, so they are non-existent and have no fixity before their existence. And the commentator refuted the Mu'tazila by his saying: 'The non-existent absolutely is not a thing,' contrary to the Mu'tazila, for the non-existent according to them is a thing, because the reality of the non-existent is fixed in itself, so it is neither pure non-existent nor pure existent. According to them, fixity in existence may accompany existence or may not accompany it, unlike according to Ahl al-Sunna, for that which is fixed in itself is existent in external existence, upon the verification of denying states.
Source pages p. 579

Commentary
This passage combines a definition and a refutation. It begins by presenting the foundational matn: the term 'thing' is applicable only to what exists; non-existence is not a thing and has no external fixity. The reason given is that existence is identical to reality (for al-Ash'ari), so removing existence removes reality. The matn then asserts that there is no intermediate state between existence and non-existence, and this is known by necessary rational judgment. The commentary then explains the disagreement with the Mu'tazila. The commentator notes a key dispute: whether possible realities have a prior fixity before existence (Mu'tazila) or are purely non-existent until created (Ahl al-Sunna). The Mu'tazila view that non-existent essences are 'things' fixed in themselves is rejected. The commentator clarifies that for the Mu'tazila, fixity in external existence can be without actual existence, while for Ahl al-Sunna, fixity in itself implies existence. The passage thus defines 'thing' strictly as existent and refutes the opposing view by appealing to the necessary judgment of reason.

Key Terms
شيء
موجود
معدوم
ثبوت
وجود
حقيقة
الضرورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between 'thing' and 'existent'?
A) They are unrelated.
B) They are synonymous and coextensive.
C) 'Thing' is broader than 'existent'.
D) 'Existent' is broader than 'thing'.

Key Takeaway
In Sunni theology, to be a 'thing' is to be existent; non-existence is absolute nothingness with no fixity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If non-existence is absolute nothingness with no fixity, what does that mean for your attachment to worldly things that will inevitably cease? Do you truly believe they are nothing once gone, or do you hold onto them in your heart as if they still have reality?
?
This passage says that existence is the very reality. Your existence right now is a gift from Allah. How does this awareness change the way you use your time and breath? Will you live today as if your existence is the only reality you have, mindful of Allah who gives it?
?
The author says this truth is known by necessity. Yet your daily choices often reflect a belief that non-existent possibilities are 'things' to be worried about. When you fear a future that does not yet exist, are you contradicting this necessary judgment? How can you align your heart with the reality that only what exists is a thing?

Refuting the Mu'tazila on Non-Existent Essences
Sanusi's commentator explains and refutes the Mu'tazili doctrine of fixed non-existent essences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazili view that possible essences are fixed before existence and the Sunni refutation that non-existence is not a thing.

Core Idea
Possible essences have no reality before creation; only the existent is real.

This lesson delves into the sectarian disagreement over the status of things before they exist. The Mu'tazila claimed that the essences of possible things are fixed in themselves prior to creation, and creation merely brings them into appearance. The Ahl al-Sunna rejected this, asserting that things have no fixity before existence. The passage refutes the Mu'tazila by affirming that the non-existent is absolutely nothing.

Guided Path
1
Learn the Mu'tazili view
Read about the first view: the Mu'tazila say possible realities are fixed in themselves, like goods hidden in a chest. They are 'things' even before existence.
This is the view being refuted.
2
Learn the Sunni view
Read about the second view: Ahl al-Sunna say realities come into being by a maker. Before existence, they are nothing – no fixity.
This is the correct position according to the commentator.
3
Understand the refutation
The commentator says: 'the non-existent absolutely is not a thing' – directly opposing the Mu'tazila. Note the reasoning: if something were fixed in itself, it would be existent, but non-existence implies no fixity.
The argument hinges on the identification of existence with reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات. فكل شيء موجود، وكل موجود شيء، والمعدوم مطلقا ـ ممكنا كان أو ممتنعا ـ ليس بشيء، ولا ثابت في الخارج؛ لأن الوجود نفس الحقيقة، فرفعه رفعها، ولا واسطة بين الموجود والمعدوم، وهذا الحكم ثابت عندنا بالضرورة؛ فإنها قاضية بذلك، إذ لا يعقل من الثبوت إلا الوجود خارجا أو ذهنا، ولا من العدم إلا نفي الوجود كذلك.
وقوله: (والمعدوم مطلقا) اختلف هل الأشياء قبل وجودها ثابتة في نفس الأمر وطرأ عليها الوجود؛ فهي قديمة والقدرة لم تتعلق إلا بوجودها وإظهارها، أو أنها قبل وجودها لم يكن لها ثبوت في نفس الأمر، بل كانت معدومة وتعلقت القدرة بإيجاد ذواتها؟ فذهبت المعتزلة إلى الأول، فقالوا: الحقائق الممكنة ليست بجعل جاعل، بل الحقيقة ثابتة في نفسها إلا أنها مستترة كاستتار المتاع في الصندوق، فهي ثابتة قبل وجودها وتعلقت القدرة بوجودها وظهورها، وإلى الثاني ذهب أهل السنة فقالوا: إن الحقائق بجعل جاعل، فهي معدومة ولا ثبوت لها قبل وجودها. والشارح رد على المعتزلة بقوله: والمعدوم مطلقا ليس بشيء خلافا للمعتزلة، فإن المعدوم عندهم شيء، لأن حقيقة المعدوم ثابتة في نفسها فليست معدوما صرفا ولا موجودا صرفا، فعندهم الثبوت في الخارج قد يجامع الوجود وقد لا يجامعه، بخلافه عند أهل السنة فإن الثابت في نفسه موجود في الخارج على التحقيق من نفي الأحوال.
Section of the Sam'iyyat. Every thing is existent, and every existent is a thing, and the non-existent absolutely — whether possible or impossible — is not a thing, nor is it fixed in external existence; because existence is the very reality, so its removal is its removal, and there is no intermediate between the existent and the non-existent, and this judgment is established with us by necessity; for necessity judges that, since no fixity is conceivable except existence externally or mentally, nor non-existence except negation of existence likewise.
And his saying: 'and the non-existent absolutely' — there is disagreement: Are things before their existence fixed in themselves and existence supervened upon them, so they are eternal and power is only connected with their existence and manifestation? Or were they before their existence not fixed in themselves, but rather non-existent, and power is connected with bringing their essences into existence? The Mu'tazila went to the first view, saying: The possible realities are not by a maker, but the reality is fixed in itself except that it is hidden like the hiding of goods in a chest; thus they are fixed before their existence and power is connected with their existence and manifestation. And the Ahl al-Sunna went to the second view, saying: Realities are by a maker, so they are non-existent and have no fixity before their existence. And the commentator refuted the Mu'tazila by his saying: 'The non-existent absolutely is not a thing,' contrary to the Mu'tazila, for the non-existent according to them is a thing, because the reality of the non-existent is fixed in itself, so it is neither pure non-existent nor pure existent. According to them, fixity in existence may accompany existence or may not accompany it, unlike according to Ahl al-Sunna, for that which is fixed in itself is existent in external existence, upon the verification of denying states.
Source pages p. 579

Commentary
This passage combines a definition and a refutation. It begins by presenting the foundational matn: the term 'thing' is applicable only to what exists; non-existence is not a thing and has no external fixity. The reason given is that existence is identical to reality (for al-Ash'ari), so removing existence removes reality. The matn then asserts that there is no intermediate state between existence and non-existence, and this is known by necessary rational judgment. The commentary then explains the disagreement with the Mu'tazila. The commentator notes a key dispute: whether possible realities have a prior fixity before existence (Mu'tazila) or are purely non-existent until created (Ahl al-Sunna). The Mu'tazila view that non-existent essences are 'things' fixed in themselves is rejected. The commentator clarifies that for the Mu'tazila, fixity in external existence can be without actual existence, while for Ahl al-Sunna, fixity in itself implies existence. The passage thus defines 'thing' strictly as existent and refutes the opposing view by appealing to the necessary judgment of reason.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
أهل السنة
ثبوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Possible essences have a real fixed existence before they are created.
Correction: According to Ahl al-Sunna, they have no fixity at all before existence; they are purely non-existent.

Checkpoint
How do the Mu'tazila describe the state of possible essences before existence?
A) They are completely non-existent.
B) They are fixed in themselves like goods hidden in a chest.
C) They exist only in the mind.
D) They are impossible.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni refutation of the Mu'tazila on non-existent essences hinges on the identification of 'thing' with 'existent' – there is no third category.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever treat your own plans or future possibilities as if they have a fixed reality independent of God's will? How does this lesson challenge you to see them as truly non-existent until God creates them?
?
The Mu'tazila thought a thing could be real without being existent. Where in your life do you treat fears, worries, or past events as having a reality that competes with God's present sovereignty? What concrete step can you take to surrender that imagined reality to God?
?
If your entire existence is a continual act of God's creation—nothing in you is self-subsisting—how does that reshape your understanding of your identity, achievements, and even your sins? Will you live today in conscious dependence on His bringing you into existence at every moment?
